National Goods Factories Request Four Items 187

Municipal Government Orders Social Affairs Bureau to Handle 188

Curb Labor Unrest, Order the Sale of National Goods

Assist Distressed Factories, Relieve Unemployment: The Shanghai United Machine-Made National Goods Factories, due to the severe impact on the social economy since the September 18th Incident, have experienced sluggish sales and financial difficulties. Some factories have been forced to downsize to survive, but layoffs have often led to labor disputes. Although the responsible authorities have mediated in accordance with the law, workers often exploit their numbers and make excessive demands. As a result, the factories have not only been unable to compensate for the losses from the Shanghai War, but also face a precarious future. Yu Xueyang, Chu Wenqi, Pan Xusheng, Xiang Kangyuan, and others were delegated to petition the Municipal Government, the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and other agencies, requesting: (1) efforts to curb labor unrest, (2) an order to sell national goods throughout the country, (3) appropriate assistance to distressed factories, and (4) prompt allocation of funds to relieve unemployment. Regarding labor disputes, at a minimum, legal sanctions should be imposed to eliminate disputes. Measures must be taken to ensure that factories have full protection and that workers never face unemployment, which would greatly benefit the future of Chinese industry. It is heard that the Municipal Government has instructed the Social Affairs Bureau to promptly verify and reply, and has issued the original petition and a copy of the dispute facts.

Social Affairs Bureau Stipulates 189

Methods for Industries to Set Prices 190

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday instructed the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, stating that for the sake of informing the relevant authorities, the procedures for industry associations to set prices have been stipulated by the Bureau as follows: (1) The price list for each industry should be decided by a meeting of member representatives. Otherwise, it should be approved by a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees of each association. If there is no supervisory committee and it is difficult to convene a meeting of member representatives, it should be approved by the executive committee at a minimum. (2) If each association has an evaluation committee, it should submit the evaluation committee to the Bureau for record in advance. (3) Each price should list the costs, expenses, and profits, either as percentages or as actual numbers, for review. In addition to separate orders, this order is issued for your information.

Russian Recklessly Drives Tram, Causes Accident 196

Coppersmith Chen Yongqing Killed in Accident

Union Holds Emergency Meeting Yesterday morning at 4:45 AM, Chen Yongqing, a night shift coppersmith at the French Concession Water and Electricity Company's old workshop, was dispatched to connect a tramcar. At that time, a certain Russian forcefully commandeered the tramcar. Because he did not know how to operate it, he turned on the power, and Chen, who was connecting the car, was hit and his head was shattered, resulting in immediate death. The police transported the body to the morgue and detained the Russian. The factory's workers were extremely angry, and the union immediately convened an emergency meeting and instructed Chen's family to attend. They resolved to demand: (1) a funeral allowance of 1,000 yuan, (2) the company to continue paying his salary monthly for 16 years, and (3) the expulsion of all White Russian workers from the factory.

Yihe Rubber Factory Labor Dispute 197

Mediated at the Social Affairs Bureau Yesterday 198

Investigate the Facts of Both Sides and Thoroughly Examine the Factory's Accounts

Temporarily Issue 5 Yuan in Living Expenses to Dismissed Workers: The labor dispute at the Nanshi Yihe Rubber Factory has been mediated by the Social Affairs Bureau several times without success. Peng Zhenqiu of the Social Affairs Bureau's Third Section advised both parties on Saturday (the 6th) to negotiate on their own and scheduled another round of negotiations for the 9th (yesterday). Yesterday, representatives from both sides arrived at the Bureau on time. At 2:00 PM, a negotiation meeting was held in the Bureau's conference room. The attendees included factory representatives Su Gongxuan and Zhang Bolun, representatives from the industry association Cai Chunfang and Shen Mengshi, and labor representatives Zheng Gengfu and Mei Shidu. Peng Zhenqiu presided over the meeting and first held a round of consultations, followed by both sides listing various facts, with lengthy debates. Peng then proposed two solutions, one non-thorough and one thorough. The non-thorough solution involved persuading both sides to make slight concessions in the spirit of labor-management cooperation, with the factory reinstating all sixteen dismissed workers and the workers ceasing any further disputes, thereby ending the conflict. The thorough solution acknowledged that if both sides were unwilling to compromise, there would be no end in sight. The Bureau would assign specialists and accountants to investigate the facts of the case and thoroughly examine the factory's accounts, and then make a fair decision based on this. If the factory was found to be at fault, it would be dealt with according to the law. Similarly, if the labor side was found to have engaged in absenteeism or other actions, the factory would be allowed to dismiss them unconditionally. As for the issue of bonus payments, this would be determined after reviewing the accounts to see if there was any surplus. Both sides agreed to adopt the thorough solution. The workers also requested that the factory first issue wages for May and June and last year's bonus during the investigation period to maintain their livelihoods after unemployment. Peng, in his personal capacity, advised the factory to consider the suffering of the unemployed workers and provide a small amount of money to support their lives. The factory agreed to provide 5 yuan per person, to be collected at Su Gongxuan's house between 8:00 and 9:00 AM this morning, and arranged to further discuss the solution at this time.

Taxpayers Association Sends Another Letter to the Engineering Bureau 201

Please Correct Tap Water Charges 202

More Than Seven Times Higher Than Before

How Can the People Bear It in This Time of Economic Distress: The Public Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association sent another letter to the General Office of the Engineering Bureau yesterday regarding tap water, saying: I am writing to inform you that the Ningbo Association in Shanghai wrote to us stating that since our association installed water meters from the Shanghai Tap Water Company, the water bill for July was more than seven times higher than the previous June. The company disregards public welfare and only seeks its own interests, which is regrettable. At a time when the people are suffering and the economy is on the verge of collapse, how can we bear further burdens? The association stated that it has only increased by more than double, but to the best of our knowledge, there are cases where it has increased by more than seven times. If this is not corrected, it will inevitably lead to the following results: either saving water, which will harm residents' health, or causing major disputes. Due to the above-mentioned reasons, we are writing to request that you quickly correct it. Respectfully addressed to the General Office of the Shanghai Public Concession Engineering Bureau. (New Sound Society)

Parts of the Company's Articles of Association that Conflict 203

Should be Amended in Accordance with the Company Law 204

The extension of the deadline will be extended for another six months from July. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce issued a notice to all members yesterday, stating that it had received an order from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce had issued an order, Business Letter No. 12611, stating that if there are any conflicts between the company's articles of association and the Company Law, they should be amended and submitted for approval within six months after the implementation of the Company Law. As the deadline of the end of December 20th was approaching, the reasons for the extension were prepared and submitted to the Executive Yuan, which approved the extension for six months and instructed the Ministry to notify the provincial and municipal governments to comply. It is now found that this deadline will expire again on June 30th of this year. Many companies in various regions have made corrections accordingly, but there are still many companies that have not been able to make the corrections on time due to various difficulties. Moreover, the company's articles of association were originally approved as valid documents, and there was nothing wrong with them according to the old law. The legal deadline for amendment is because the new law has been implemented, and it cannot be allowed to conflict with it permanently. The short deadline is intended to make everyone comply with the new law as soon as possible. Now, because it is impossible to complete the amendments on time, in order to consider the difficulties of businesses and to make all companies' articles of association comply with the new law, the Executive Yuan's Order No. 1838 was issued again, approving a further extension of six months from July 1st of this year, etc. In addition to separate orders, we are ordering you to forward this order to all companies that have not yet amended their articles of association in accordance with the law, to comply and amend them as soon as possible, and submit them to avoid further delays. We are ordering you to follow these instructions and to forward them to all members for compliance.

Chinese Goods Transported to Vietnam Must be Inspected 205

The French Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Merry Ai, has been in effect since July 2, and yesterday wrote to the Municipal Government, saying: I am writing to inform you that the Governor of Vietnam has now issued an order that, from July 2 of this year, all goods transported from Shanghai to Vietnam must be inspected to prevent the transmission of typhoid bacteria, etc. I am writing to request that Your Honor investigate and inform the competent authorities.

Shipping News 206

The Sanbei Liner to be Adjusted to the Chongqing-Yichang Route: The Chongqing-Yichang route of the Sanbei Company, originally served by the Wuxing and Fuyang liners, has been affected. After the Wuxing liner encountered an accident at Chenglingji last month, only the Fuyang liner remained in operation, resulting in a lack of scheduled voyages. Ren Duqing, the manager in Yichang, recognizing this issue, telegraphed the head office requesting additional sailings. Upon receiving the telegram, the head office decided to transfer the Tianbei liner, which had been operating on the Ningbo-Zhoushan-Puzi route, to the Chongqing-Yichang route. This liner arrived in Shanghai in the middle of last month for repairs, which have now been completed, and it is scheduled to depart for Yichang this morning. After the sinking of the Wuxing liner, salvage operations were impossible due to high water levels. Attempts will be made to salvage the vessel once the water recedes.

The Shengjing Liner Repairs Completed and Returns to Service on the Taikoo Northern Route: The new Shengjing liner of the Taikoo Northern Route sailed from Shanghai to Tianjin for the ninth time last month. While sailing near Qingming Island near Weihaiwei, it struck a reef in the fog. After being towed out, it returned to Shanghai for repairs, which have lasted more than a month. The company received a telegram from the Hong Kong head office the other day stating that the repairs have been completed, and it is approved to return to service from Hong Kong to Shanghai on the ninth. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai for Weihaiwei, Yantai, and Tianjin at 10:00 AM on the thirteenth.

The Dayu Liner Returns to Service After Annual Repairs: The Dayu liner of the Dada Company's Tongyang route underwent its annual repairs at the beginning of last month as scheduled. The repairs have now been completed. The liner was originally a new vessel, and it has become even more magnificent and luxurious after these repairs. The passenger cabins are spacious, and all facilities are complete, including a grand dining room, rest rooms, and more, making it the finest on the Tongyang route.

Organizing a National Goods Consumer Cooperative 207

Initiated by Du Gang and Others

Adopting the Rochdale Principles: Since the September 18th Incident in the Northeast, the people of the entire nation have been extremely indignant, advocating for economic severance and boycotting enemy goods as a form of resistance. To this day, the blood of our oaths has not yet dried, but some unscrupulous merchants only seek profit, often passing off enemy goods as domestic goods, deceiving themselves and others. This has led to a lack of identification capabilities for patriotic citizens, who are unable to avoid buying enemy goods even if they desire to do so. Du Gang, Xu Jiashi, Du Mengsen, and others, recognizing that enemy goods may never be completely eliminated if this continues, have initiated the organization of a National Goods Consumer Cooperative as a fundamental means of resistance. Since the news spread, more than fifty people have requested to join as initiators, and the number continues to grow. It is reported that the cooperative is tentatively named the "Greater Shanghai Limited Consumer Cooperative." Draft articles of association have been prepared, adopting the principles of the British Rochdale Equitable Pioneers Society, setting the share capital at five yuan per share, with each member required to subscribe to at least one share. A preparatory office has been established at 118 Rue Lupan in the French Concession. It is also heard that the future location of the cooperative is planned to be in the central area of the French Concession, and branch cooperatives or offices will be established in various locations as the cooperative develops. This type of organization is the best method for resisting enemy goods, and the China Cooperative Society is also very appreciative and willing to help.

Local Court 208

Today's Burning of Narcotics 209

The Procuratorate of the Shanghai Local Court will, as usual, conduct a semi-annual closure of all opium cases confiscated in the second half of the twentieth year, including opium, opium paste, morphine, heroin, red pills, smoking paraphernalia, and so on, totaling 4,948 items. It has submitted a request to the Jiangsu Higher Court Procuratorate for instructions, and it has been decided to burn them on the morning of the tenth of this month. Chief Prosecutor Liu Maochu, after receiving the order, has complied and ordered the director of the evidence storage to number, identify, and list the items, and has issued a notice and sent letters to various agencies, requesting them to send personnel to supervise the burning today.

Simalu Businessmen's Association 210

Supporting the Party Headquarters' Rent Reduction Proposal 211

The Simalu Businessmen's Association and the 20th District Branch of the Citizens' Union have issued a declaration in support of the Shanghai Party Headquarters' proposal to reduce or waive rent:

Page 16

The prosperity of the city's commerce and the density of the population are unparalleled in the nation. Demand exceeds supply, and it is further manipulated by some unbenevolent wealthy merchants. As a result, rents have been increasing day by day, with rent alone accounting for half of all expenditures, especially in our central district. In normal times, with a prosperous market and good business, we can barely maintain our livelihood by tightening our belts and working hard. However, with two months of market closures and spending continuing, coupled with a sluggish market and plummeting business after the war, we are economizing on food and clothing to survive, while rent remains as high as ever, without any reduction due to the economic difficulties of society or any exemption for the inability of citizens to live in peace. How can this be fair in law or in principle? The city government's proposed rent reduction or waiver measures are indeed biased and unfair, disregarding the merchants and residents of our central district. The city party headquarters can consider the hardships of the merchants and seek welfare for the common people, and thus has petitioned the National Government to send personnel to Shanghai to jointly re-establish rent reduction standards with party and government agencies and mass organizations. This proposal truly understands the suffering of the merchants and residents, and the members of this association express their deepest sympathy and will definitely support its implementation to alleviate the suffering of our merchants and residents and restore the former prosperity of the market. We hereby declare.

Roulette Den 215

Investigating the Head of the Outfit 216

French Concession police detectives previously cracked a roulette gambling den at 809 Route Cardinal Mercier, seizing gambling equipment and smoking paraphernalia, and arresting twenty-seven people, including Russian Bai Xigaofu and Chinese Chen Jiande, who were sent to the court. Since Wang was unable to pay the cash, he submitted a request to change the bail to shop bail, which was approved yesterday.

After the Paramour was Shot and Killed 217

The Family Sues the Husband 218

Seeking Damages of More Than 13,000 Yuan: Yao Guishan, a local resident who lived at Wangjiatai, Gaolang Bridge, and worked as a rattan chair maker, had an affair with Wang Wanshi, the wife of Wang Xingsheng, a carpenter. In March of this year, he abducted her to Zhoupu, Pudong, to live together. Wang found her and took her back. On July 3, Yao met Wang Wanshi outside Xiaodongmen, Shiliupu, to arrange a secret meeting at the Oriental Hotel. The husband found out, carried a handgun, chased them to No. 33 Yuxing Street, Xiaodongmen, French Concession, and fired two shots at Yao's back, hitting him in the waist and buttocks. The patrol police arrested the husband, Wang, recovered the handgun and bullets, and took him to the police station. Yao was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment. The husband and wife were sent to the Second Special Court for investigation. Yao died on the fourth of this month due to his injuries. The prosecutor examined the body and the body was claimed. This case was heard yesterday by Judge Wang Gangxi and Prosecutor Wu Xiaoke in the Criminal Division. The police first prosecuted for assault, but now changed the charges to assault causing death. The plaintiff, Yao's father, Yao Jiahai, hired lawyer Xue Jiaqi as an agent and requested incidental civil compensation of 6,000 yuan for the deceased's loss of life, 3,240 yuan for the deceased's two daughters' living expenses, 500 yuan for the deceased's funeral expenses, and 3,840 yuan for the deceased's father's support, totaling 13,580 yuan, and stated that the defendant had several acres of land in Yinxiang Port, worth 5,000-6,000 yuan per acre, and that the defendant had the ability to pay the incidental civil suit. The court questioned the details of the affair, the abduction, and the intention to harm the victim. The defendant's lawyers, Zhang Ji and Qin Zemin, stated that the facts of the case were clear, that the debate could be opened today, and there was no need to postpone it. Regarding the private prosecution, the defendant did not have the financial ability to bear such a huge loss. The court ordered the hearing to be adjourned. The lawyers for both parties were ordered to settle the private prosecution out of court.

Qingfu Pawnshop 219

The Case of the Young Owner Killing Two Partners 220

Yesterday, the First Special Court opened the trial of Weng Yuanzhen, the young owner of Qingfu Pawnshop at No. 2649 Yangshupu Road, Shanghai, who, on June 18, killed his two partners, Jiang Zhenfang from Huizhou and Li Guannan from Luodian, because of the embezzlement of funds. The victims' families directly hired lawyers Xu Kaixian and Zhang Henghai to file a lawsuit with the First Special Court, requesting the arrest and severe punishment of the murderers and demanding compensation from Weng Yongjun (the murderer Weng Yuanzhen's father) in the Civil Division to maintain the livelihood of the victims' families. Unexpectedly, Weng Yongjun published a notice in the newspaper the other day, entrusting lawyers to hastily declare liquidation, apparently trying to conceal assets and escape all legal responsibility. The family had no choice but to ask Fang Peiqing, a relative in Shanghai, to represent them and appeal to all sectors of society, uniting lawyers Xu and Zhang to expedite legal procedures, while publishing a rebuttal in the newspaper, denying the liquidation. It is learned that Fang, out of familial ties and a sense of duty, invited friends and relatives of Jiang and Li, including Zhang Zhizhi and Sun Wenhai, to No. 1246 Huade Road the other day to discuss ways to proceed. It was resolved to organize the Jiang Li Massacre Shanghai Relatives Support Association to provide strong assistance, and a declaration was issued, describing the truth of the massacre and requesting practical assistance from all organizations and local fair-minded people. A temporary contact address was set up at No. 1246 Huade Road. It is also learned that the case was opened in the First Special Court yesterday morning, and the lawyers for both parties were present in court. The plaintiff's lawyer Xu requested that the defendant's business records for the past years be reviewed to preserve evidence, which was approved by the court and a date for a retrial was set.

Jinghu (Shanghai-Nanjing) Railway 221

The Cargo Warehouse at North Station Was Robbed 222

At about 7:45 PM last night, three robbers, speaking with a Jiangbei accent, all in their thirties and wearing blue cloth shirts and carrying three Browning handguns, rushed into the stationmaster's office through the back door of the freight station. They pointed their guns at the staff members Cao Qinghong and Zhou Jiadong, shouting to prevent them from making any noise. They drove Cao and Zhou into a room and began to search. After about a few minutes, they walked out the front door and left. The total amount of freight money stolen was 424.90 yuan. The bureau chief has been notified. As the robbery occurred in broad daylight, which is extremely unlawful, the head of the Shanghai section police has been ordered to solve the case within a time limit.

Verdict on the Sweater Theft Case 223

The Thief and the Receiver of Stolen Goods are Both Convicted: Yang Chongyuan, a clerk at the Beihengmao Customs Brokerage at No. 59 Guangdong Road, successively colluded with his uncle Yang Yushan to steal 116 sweaters entrusted to the brokerage for customs clearance, which they then sold and split the profits. After the owner noticed the theft, he reported it to the General Police Station, which sent Detective Song Yuanshan and Detective Huang Fusen to arrest the two Yangs. It was also determined that the stolen goods were privately received by the Huaxin Company on Yinhua Street, Nanjing Road. After searching the company, the police found 102 original stolen sweaters. The missing 14 items had already been sold. The police charged Liang Zhengpei, the manager of Huaxin, with receiving stolen goods, and charged the two Yangs with joint theft, and filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Local Court.

Yesterday morning, Judge Liu opened a retrial. Police lawyer Hu Jiabao stated that the case had been thoroughly investigated, the evidence was conclusive, and he requested severe punishment. Liang Zhengpei still tried to evade responsibility and hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng for defense. Judge Liu finished the hearing and immediately announced the verdict: Yang Chongyuan was sentenced to six months in prison, Yang Yushan was sentenced to four months in prison, Liang Zhengpei was fined 400 yuan, and the stolen goods were returned to the original owner for collection. The value of the 14 sold items must be compensated. As Liang declared he was not satisfied with the verdict and would appeal, the court ordered the stolen goods to be temporarily stored at the police station pending review by the Court of Appeal.

Autopsy of a Young Woman Who Committed Suicide by Poisoning 224

The woman Sun Jiang, 20 years old, from Ningbo, resided at No. 448 Rue Au Ga. The other night, she had an argument with her husband while cooling off on the sundeck. Feeling resentful, she wanted to end her life and swallowed opium smoke without anyone knowing. The next morning, her aunt Sun Shen and others found her and took her to the Gu Long Hospital for treatment. She died at 5:00 PM that afternoon. The hospital reported it to the Jiaxing Road Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the Forensic Center on Feren Road. Yesterday morning, Inspector Guo, appointed by the First Special District Local Court, examined the body and conducted a court session. Sun Shen stated that her family ran a steel shop, and the deceased was her daughter-in-law. That day, when the two of them were cooling off, her son was lying on the couch, and the deceased was sitting next to him. Later, her son asked the deceased to get clothes, and an argument broke out. The deceased's father, Jiang Lianqing, 47 years old, from Ningbo, a Jinghua merchant from Shiliupu in the South City, stated that his daughter had been married for two years, but she had only returned home twice, and returned to her husband's home on the same day. He had repeatedly gone to their home, but had never seen his daughter. Their family was very secretive and mistreated his daughter. Her husband has now fled. He requested the Inspector to seek justice. After hearing the statements, Inspector Guo ruled that Sun Jiang had committed suicide by opium poisoning and ordered the body to be handed over to her aunt Sun Shen for burial.

500 Rounds of Ammunition Seized 225

Purchased from a French Ship: He Kaifei, a Cantonese man, was found to be carrying prohibited handgun ammunition at about 2:00 PM the day before yesterday. While riding in a rickshaw, traveling on Broadway, he was spotted by Chinese detective Feng Shuofu, who found his appearance suspicious and stopped him immediately. A bag of bullets was found on him, with twenty-five rounds in each box, a total of twenty boxes of bullets. He was taken to the police station. He confessed that he had been working as a chief steward on the French Merchant Godtese liner for three years. He had purchased the ammunition from France for 7 yuan per hundred rounds. After the ship arrived in Shanghai on the 7th of this month, he went to the Banjuqing Amusement Club at No. 450 Wuchang Road to play, and met a friend named A Liang, who asked if he had any ammunition for sale. He said he only had 500 rounds, and it was agreed that the price would be 10 yuan per hundred rounds, and they would be delivered that day. Unexpectedly, he was arrested en route. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Fourth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, where he was questioned by Judge Fu. Police lawyer Chen Ming narrated the situation and presented the ammunition. When questioned, the defendant claimed that he was selling the ammunition for someone else for the first time, and did not know it was illegal. Judge Fu ordered the defendant to be detained and the hearing adjourned.

Gaoqiao Municipal Committee member Zhong Renjie submitted a letter to the Municipal Government yesterday, stating that he was resigning for a continuation and asking to be replaced with an alternate. After reading this, I was terrified. Now, at the time of strict local autonomy, to promote post-war municipal administration, Renjie's commercial position, more and more often to leave Shanghai, delay back and forth, it is difficult to deal with. If the delay continues, private and public distress, neither benefits the city, more hinders the person, must the Superior consider the foolish heart, to resign from the position of municipal committee of Gaoqiao District, Renjie deeply desires to retire to the position of citizen, still to be able to see what is heard, at any time to assist the city. Letter Received

To the Editor:

Having read the news published in yesterday's (9th) edition of your newspaper under the heading ("The Zhu Shaoyi Case: Disputes Intensify"), which included a subheading ("Anti-Zhu Faction Workers Assault Neutral Faction Workers"), we find the content to be factually inaccurate and deeply disconcerting. The anti-Zhu movement is purely the result of the majority of workers being unable to bear the oppression of Zhu Shaoyi, leading to a united uprising under the leadership of the entire labor union. There is no distinction between an "anti-Zhu faction" and a "neutral faction." Furthermore, since Lu Jiyun and Chuan Chongde are responsible personnel of the labor union and did not participate in the work of posting slogans and distributing leaflets, the entire labor union is naturally responsible and has nothing to do with Lu and Chuan. As for Zhang Ruoyu, Hu Ruizhang, Zhan Yongyi, etc., who were allegedly assaulted and falsely accused union members in court, whether they were actually assaulted is questionable. Your newspaper's claim that the dispute is intensifying is entirely inconsistent with the facts, and we are concerned that it may mislead various circles. Therefore, we specifically request that your newspaper promptly make corrections to clarify the truth. We are deeply hopeful.

Sincerely,

First District Water and Electricity Industry Labor Union, August 9th.

A Little Chat

六脈渠 239

**Six Meridian Canals**

— Zhan Lu

Guangzhou has been struck by devastating rainstorms, breaking decades-old records! According to reports in the Guangdong newspapers, countless citizens have drowned and countless houses have collapsed. The pitiful Home for the Elderly has been turned into a crystal palace! The lonely old men and women have all become drowned rats! Statistics show that more than three hundred people have drowned in the two male and female residences, not including other affected citizens. One can only hum two lines of classical text: "The heartbreaking scene is truly like this?"

An investigation into the cause of the disaster reveals that the problem lies in the poor drainage of the canals. The canals that Guangzhou relies on to drain rainwater are called the "Six Meridian Canals." The name "Six Meridian" is well chosen: if a person's six meridians are out of balance, the person will fall ill; if the water's six meridians are blocked, the water will overflow. In the past, the municipal authorities always treated dredging the six meridian canals as an important task. But now, the officials in charge of public works have actually narrowed the main canal and tightened its mouth; with a narrow mouth, the excessive amount of rainwater cannot be drained in time, and this unprecedented tragedy has occurred! Therefore, the word "violent" in the "violent rain disaster" is simply unfair to the Rain Master; the rain is not violent, it is the officials who narrowed the canal mouth who are violent. I think that the tangible six meridian canals must be dredged at all times, and the intangible six meridian canals cannot be tightened. The more open and accessible all public opinion and media organizations are, the clearer the political situation will be. If they also adopt a narrowing policy and tighten their mouths, then preventing the people's speech is more dangerous than preventing a river. The intangible violent rain disaster is even more unmanageable than the tangible violent rain disaster.

The overflow of Guangzhou's Six Meridian Canals is a good lesson for the government officials to learn.

死守江陰乃閻典 240

**Yan, the Historian Who Defended Jiangyin**

— Shi Junshuo

Mr. Wang Yi-wu recounts the story of Yan, the Recorder, who defended Jiangyin. (Mr. Wang mistakenly referred to Yan as Yan). The intention is to commend the loyalty and patriotism of the Northeast Volunteers, and to hate the unpatriotic officials in high positions who lack integrity. He hopes that they will be grateful to the volunteer army and be able to regain lost territory by force, which is well-intentioned. However, the surname of Yan, the Recorder, was mistaken, and his given name, place of origin, and the events of his arrival in Jiangyin to protect the area were not detailed. Therefore, I will fill in the gaps for the benefit of the newspaper readers, so that those who admire heroes will have something to study. According to the Biography of Yan Ying-yuan, the Recorder of Shaoqingmen, Yan, the Recorder, whose name was Ying-yuan and courtesy name was Li-heng, was originally from Shaoxing, Zhejiang, and later his family settled in Tongzhou, Zhili. Ying-yuan started as a clerk and served as an official in the Beijing Granary. In the fourteenth year of Chongzhen, he was transferred to Jiangyin as a recorder. When he first arrived, there were a hundred Jiangyin pirates, who set up banners and took advantage of the tide to enter the interior, approaching the city. The county magistrate was temporarily governing a neighboring county, and the officials were fleeing. Men and women ran away. Ying-yuan went out with a sword and quiver, and shouted from his horse in the market: "Good men, follow me to kill the bandits and protect your families!" At that time, a thousand people followed him. But there were no banners. Ying-yuan then rushed to the bamboo shop and shouted: "The situation is urgent! Lend me a pole each!" A thousand people stood on the riverbank, their spears like a forest, the soldiers like a wall. Ying-yuan rode back and forth, shooting arrows. Each arrow killed a bandit. Three bandits were killed in a row, and the pirates were so frightened that they lowered their sails and left. (Nowadays, bandits and thieves abound. The officials who govern this land usually send troops and police to pursue after the bandits have looted and fled far away. Should they not be ashamed to death compared to Yan, the Recorder?) Later, Ying-yuan was promoted to a registrar in a certain county in Guangdong, but he did not go due to his mother's illness. When the national crisis occurred, he took his family to live in Shanshan, east of the county. (The following is a slightly abridged version.) The Prince Regent's army crossed the Yangtze River and sent princes and other generals to pacify the southeastern counties. From Jingkou onwards, in one month, they captured hundreds of famous cities and counties. Jiangyin, a small town, held out for more than eighty days before falling. Ying-yuan's plans were mostly responsible for this. At first, when the shaving order was issued, the students, led by Xu Yong-de, cried in the Minglun Hall. Tens of thousands of people gathered, wanting to support County Lieutenant Chen Ming-xuan to defend the city. Ming-xuan said, "My wisdom and courage are not as good as Mr. Yan's. This is a major matter. Mr. Yan must come." So he rode at night to welcome Ying-yuan. Ying-yuan got up and rushed to the city with his family at night. After preparing the necessary equipment, he divided the city to defend it. Wu Ju Huang Lue defended the east gate, Bazong defended the south gate, Chen Mingxuan defended the west gate, and Yingyuan defended the north gate. After the deployment was completed, the city was surrounded. The city was defended for eighty-one days. The main army surrounded the city with 250,000 troops, and 67,000 died. Another 7,000 died in street battles. No less than 56,000 people died in the city. Corpses were piled up everywhere, and the streets and alleys were filled. However, not a single person surrendered. In the middle, they once sent brave men to scale the walls into the camp at night and set fire to it with the wind. The army was in chaos, and many were trampled to death. The army retreated and stopped camping three miles from the city. The commander, Liu Liangzuo, rode to the city and shouted, "I have a close relationship with Mr. Yan and want to see him." Ying-yuan stood on the city and spoke to him. Liu was one of the four generals of Hongguang and was enfeoffed as the Earl of Guangchang. He had already surrendered and was now an officer. He remotely said to Ying-yuan, "Hongguang has fled, and Jiangnan has no master. Surrender early, and you can be guaranteed wealth and honor." Ying-yuan said, "I am just a recorder of the Ming Dynasty, but I still know righteousness. General, you have been given land and a fiefdom and are an important general of the country. You cannot protect Jianghuai but instead become a vanguard for the enemy. What face do you have to meet the righteous men of our city?" Liangzuo retreated in shame. Ying-yuan had a great stature, a dark complexion, a slight beard, and a strict and resolute nature. His orders were solemn and no one dared to disobey. He was generous and not stingy with rewards. When he spoke to brave men, he always called them "good brothers" instead of their names. Chen Mingxuan patrolled the city every day, comforting the soldiers and sharing their hardships, sometimes to the point of tears. Therefore, both men were able to win the hearts of the people, and the soldiers were willing to die for them. According to the Biography of Yan, the Recorder of Qingmen, there are nearly two thousand words. Here, I have excerpted the main points to show the outline of the defense of the city. As for the donation of large sums of money, Cheng Bi, a student of the Imperial College, first donated 25,000 gold as an initiative, and the donors gathered like clouds. They were all grateful for Mr. Yan's righteousness. Mr. Yan had already been promoted to an official in another province. A retired recorder still had the responsibility to defend the land like this.

There are two major academic institutions in Shanghai: the Chinese Vocational Education Society and the Chinese Study and Art Society. The former is rich in practical capabilities, while the latter has a research nature. The promotion of Chinese culture relies heavily on them. Upon arrival, Ou Zhihuai, Zhou Changshou, and others hung a big red flower and wore yellow reception ribbons to diligently welcome guests into the venue. Cai Yuanpei, Liang Shuming, Huang Yanpei, He Bocheng, and Ye Gongchuo sat solemnly on the platform, preparing for the meeting. The bell rang and the curtain opened. Could this be a case of "the older, the stronger?" Liang has recently been engaged in rural movements and hopes that the practical application of academics and art will be widespread in the countryside and have an impact. Ge Gongzhen was afraid of being dragged on stage to speak, so he slipped away halfway. The chairman couldn't find him, but the old man was in a corner of the west building, leaning against the railing and talking about the way to save the country with the members of the Newspaper Society. As the sun set, the guests visited the new building. The society occupies an area of 2.4 mu, three times larger than the Chinese Vocational Education Society. It is a modern building with a completely three-dimensional straight line design, incorporating Indian and French elements. The roof decoration is like a Christmas cake, beautiful and appetizing. The furnishings are also exquisite and modern. It is said that the design and construction were all undertaken voluntarily by member Liu Shiying, costing a total of 200,000 gold, which can be said to be cheap and beautiful. However, I dislike the auditorium's structure, as the sound does not gather well, and the platform is too small to be fully utilized. The society currently has more than twenty branches, scattered around the world like stars. There are 672 members, with each province having members, but Zhejiang accounts for the most. Among them, 463 graduates from foreign universities account for nearly two-thirds of the total. Most of them study engineering and science. There are twelve categories of publications, totaling 147 kinds, in addition to the Study and Art Magazine. The 128 Shanghai difficulties were destroyed by business affairs. They will all be looted in one day. Study art, after this, you should work harder.

西瓜之藥用談 242

**A Discussion on the Medicinal Uses of Watermelon**

— Chi Fo

Having read Mr. Shizi's "Random Talks on Watermelon" in Free Talk, which mentions that watermelon rind can be pickled and used as a side dish, but does not detail its medicinal uses, I believe he is not a true connoisseur of watermelon. Based on what I know, I will briefly mention a few things and offer my humble opinion.

Watermelon is also called "cold melon" because it originated in the Western Regions. Ouyang Xiu's "Four Barbarians Supplement" in the History of the Five Dynasties states that the Khitans, who lived in the Qidan region, first ate watermelon. It is said that the Khitans conquered the Uyghurs and obtained this species. Therefore, Xinjiang, Hami, and other places are very rich in watermelons today. Li Shizhen's "Compendium of Materia Medica" of the Ming Dynasty states that Tao Hongjing's annotations on watermelon stalks mention that Emperor Huai of Jin in Yongjia had very large cold melons that could be stored until spring. This means that watermelon seeds had already entered Zhejiang at that time, but there was no name for watermelon. There are many plants and animals that did not originate in China. Yuan Wei-zhi of the Tang Dynasty wrote a poem: "In what year did the kingdom of Anshi send pomegranates ten thousand miles as tribute?" It is said that pomegranate is also called Ruoliu or Anshi Pomegranate. Zhang Qian, the envoy of the Han Dynasty, went to the Western Regions and brought back pomegranate seeds from the kingdom of Anshi. This was the beginning of pomegranates in China. Watermelon is also similar. Li Shizhen did not study the classics and devoted himself to medicine. The "Biographies of Fangji" in the History of Ming highly praised him. The medicinal use of watermelon began with Li Shizhen.

Typhoid fever, also known as intestinal obstruction typhus, is a very dangerous disease in autumn and summer. The cause of the disease is drinking dirty water, eating too many melons and fruits, and sleeping in the open air, which allows the germs to run rampant. The fever is highest in the second and third weeks after the onset of the disease. A slight carelessness in treatment can often lead to death. Traditional Chinese medicine is more effective in treating this disease. Some medicines use cold drugs such as antelope horn and gypsum, but watermelon is the only specific drug. (Western doctors often use ice packs to treat patients with high fever, which is very dangerous and not as good as drinking watermelon juice. Also, we must never turn on the electric fan when we fall asleep, because I know that many people have died from this. Be careful, be careful!) Therefore, it is advisable to store one or two watermelons at home in autumn and winter in case of emergency. It is not only for cooling off the summer heat. My late mother fell ill with typhoid fever at an early age and almost died, but she was cured with watermelon.)

Dropsy is often caused by the kidneys failing to perform their excretory function. Watermelon has diuretic properties, so it is a special medicine for kidney disease. The method is to stuff the watermelon rind with garlic, coat the outside of the watermelon with mud, and bake it over a low fire. After the mud dries, drink the watermelon juice to treat dropsy. Some say to stuff the watermelon with rooster droppings and drink the juice, but it seems not as clean as garlic.

Cut watermelon rind into powder and mix it with lime and sesame oil to make a liquid, which is a wonderful medicine for burns. It immediately relieves pain after application and has antiseptic properties. There is a saying: "Watermelon is also known as Baihu Tang. Eating it in hot weather is harmless." This is true. However, I have heard Zhen Xishan say: "Melons and peaches are cold and should be eaten in small amounts, lest they cause malaria and dysentery in the autumn." Huang Lusu said: "People all say that watermelon can ward off the heat and do not avoid it when it is cold. But they do not know that after running around in the heat, they feel a stuffiness in their chest. If they eat it cold, although it can ward off the heat, it is ultimately harmful. If they sit in a high hall and eat it regularly, it will damage their spleen and stomach." Also, it is extremely dangerous to eat watermelon after a house party or waking up. Be careful not to think that eating watermelon to satiety is harmless. Gentlemen, please be aware. Thank you for submitting your manuscript in July. A small amount of remuneration has been prepared. Starting from today, except for Sundays and the accounting period from the 26th of each month to the 6th of the following month when payment is suspended, please come to the accounting department of this museum between 2:00 PM and 4:00 PM every day to receive it. If you collect several months of fees together, you must list them separately by month and stamp them. In the future, if you submit any more manuscripts, you must stamp them on the manuscript, regardless of the length, for verification when receiving remuneration, otherwise, the remuneration will be waived. Furthermore, in order to streamline procedures and facilitate accounting, the accounting department will set a deadline of six months from the date of publication for remuneration. If the remuneration is still not collected at that time, it will be considered that you do not wish to receive the remuneration, and the account will be cancelled. We hope you will understand. 睇嚮齋逞談 243

**Chatting in the Quiet Studio**

— Gan Yi

Wang Chonghui

Western universities call students with deep scholarship and excellent academic performance after graduation "doctors." This is not something that can be achieved by luck. But now, people who are not scholars pretend to be, and scholars who are not broad pretend to be. Thus, doctors are as numerous as feathers. Chinese people who go to Europe and America to study mostly obtain this title and return as a social ornament. When asked about the way to become a doctor, they stare blankly and cannot say a word. Even actors who occasionally show off their skills are given this elegant title and become proud. Is this the doctor's good fortune or misfortune? Wang Chonghui can truly be called a doctor who lives up to his name. His courtesy name is Liangchou and he is from Dongguan, Guangdong. He is a Doctor of Law from America. He returned to China in the year of Xinhai and was appointed as the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Provisional Government. It was unprecedented in the history of the founding of the country for a scholar to suddenly hold such a great responsibility. He held office for a short time, but his reputation was outstanding. When the government moved north and merged to form a unified government, he was appointed Minister of Justice on the recommendation of Tang Shaoyi. When Shaoyi retired, he left with him, hiding in Shanghai and working as a translator for the China Bookstore. He usually wore a Western suit and carried a cane, walking on the streets. His appearance was not striking, and those who saw him did not know that he was a high-ranking official. He was reappointed as Minister of Justice and served in the governments of Li, Feng, Xu, and Cao. During that time, he also held the reins of power with Wang Zhengting, Yan Huiqing, Huang Fu, Gu Weijun, and others, known as the New Diplomacy Faction. When Cao Kun used bribery to control the country, the people of the Privy Council often did not understand what was being discussed. Chonghui smiled silently. When asked why, he said, "For a senior official, being able to say yes during the day is already a top choice, why bother understanding things?" Others found him easy-going and were happy to be close to him. Therefore, although he was a member of the Kuomintang, he was not resented. After the party came to power, he still held judicial power. Jokers mocked him as an elder of the Six Dynasties. Hu Hanmin defended him, saying, "Chonghui served in the Northern Court for a long time, secretly observing the government's actions. (Without harming individuals, he benefits our party.) This is not something I know." Hu's words should be credible.

Extra Edition of Shen Bao Local News

Remarks

吳秀才的妙論 245

**The Brilliant Arguments of Scholar Wu**

— Fo

Since Scholar Wu telegraphed his resignation and secluded himself to study, we have not heard his high-minded arguments for a long time. Now, reading his letter to Chiang Kai-shek, urging him to quickly determine national policies, clearly promulgate a constitution, and reorganize ethical norms, etc., his words are profound, earnest, and clear. I greatly admire him, but I have both satisfied and dissatisfied views on what he says.

He says, "(Ritual and education are the mother of society, and morality has no distinction between East and West, old and new)," etc. What he considers ritual, education, and morality are still the Three Cardinal Guides, the Five Constant Virtues, the Eight Virtues, and the Nine Classics. This is, after all, too old-fashioned. In fact, the problem with China now is that after the old ritual and education were destroyed, no new ritual and education were established; after the old morality was destroyed, no new morality was inherited. Because there are good aspects of the old ritual and education, and there are bad aspects of the old ritual and education; there are good aspects of the old morality, and there are bad aspects of the old morality. In short, a country has its own ritual, education, and morality. If the old ritual and education are gone, and there is no new ritual and education, how can this become a country?

In ancient times, the sage kings established rituals and made music after achieving great achievements, to express the constitution and culture of a generation. Therefore, the Three Kings had different rituals, and the Five Emperors had different music. Rituals and education change with the times. Therefore, the old rituals and education are not applicable to modern trends. This is undeniable by anyone. As for morality, in the past, our country emphasized chivalrous morality, but now, countries emphasize broad morality. Therefore, the morality emphasized by each country is nothing more than two points: what is the highest goal of morality, and how can it be the final end of our people? If we study the history of Western ethics, we know that foreigners have never been without morality.

Now, the old ritual and education and the old morality of our country have long been overthrown. May I ask, where are the new ritual and education? Where is the new morality? In the past, husbands had the "seven grounds for divorce" against their wives, which were truly traitors to humanity. Now, there are eight or nine grounds for divorce, and there are no articles to limit them. In the past, if children were bad, parents could sue them for disobedience. Now, children can sue their parents for disobedience. The Soviet Russian Communist Party only wants to overthrow capitalism, but now anyone in our country wants to overthrow it. It is truly a case of "the superiors have no moral standards, the inferiors have no laws to follow, the guiding principles have fallen to the ground, and orders are not carried out." This cannot be blamed on the badness of the new ritual and education, but on the badness of having no ritual and education; it cannot be blamed on the badness of the new morality, but on the badness of having no morality.

Scholar Wu secludes himself to study, specializing in the study of our country's sacred scriptures and biographies of sages, and has gained some insights. However, I am afraid that he has not yet observed the root cause of the ills of the times with sufficient clarity?

科學 247

Science

Methods for Inspecting Canned Goods 248

— Zhuo Tao

Aside from bottled canned goods, where we can observe the contents through the glass to determine their quality, we have no way of inspecting the contents of ordinary cans to determine their quality. Buying canned goods is a gamble; if you get a good one, that's good, but if you get a bad one, you're out of luck. A bad can not only results in economic loss but is also harmful to health because the contents of a bad can undergo many changes and contain toxic substances. Occasionally, people inadvertently eat bad canned goods and contract various difficult-to-treat diseases. Therefore, we must be careful when buying canned goods. I will now describe the most common methods for inspecting canned goods, as follows:

1. Appearance: Since we cannot observe the contents of ordinary canned goods from the outside, nor can we open them to inspect them on the spot, we can only estimate the quality of the contents by observing the external shape of the can, specifically by observing whether the lid or bottom is bulging. If the can is thoroughly degassed during manufacturing and adequately heated, the air inside the can will be thin, and the lid and bottom should appear concave, indicating a good can. If the container is poorly manufactured, or degassing and heating are incomplete, the lid and bottom of the can will often bulge, indicating communication between the inside and outside air,

###

or that the contents have decayed and are producing gas. The appearance inspection method is generally applicable to most canned goods, except for aerated and bottled varieties.

2. Tapping: Even after an appearance inspection, it may still be impossible to determine the quality of the can. A tapping inspection is also needed before a determination can be made. For a tapping inspection, use a metal or hardwood (even a balance beam is acceptable) stick to lightly tap the lid and bottom of the can, using the clarity of the sound to distinguish the quality of the contents. The sound will vary depending on the type of contents, the preparation method, the amount of liquid, and the shape of the container. Generally, a clear, solid sound indicates a good can, while a hollow, muddy sound usually indicates a bad can.

Society Improvement Discussion Group

My Views on Improving Ancestral Worship 249

— Proposer: Huang Yingdai

Everyone has ancestors, and we often perform ancestral worship to remember them. However, I feel that modern ancestral worship is too costly. Not counting birthdays and death anniversaries, ordinary families inevitably perform ancestral worship at least six times a year: Qingming Festival, Summer Solstice, Ghost Festival (July 15th), October Festival, Winter Solstice, and New Year's Eve. When performing ancestral worship, wealthy families spend tens or hundreds of dollars, but even middle- and lower-class families spend at least two or three dollars to prepare dishes, light incense and candles, and burn tin foil. This adds up to about twenty dollars a year. Furthermore, small offerings are required on ancestors' birthdays and death anniversaries.

To this day, we have not obtained sufficient proof of the existence of ghosts, so why is it necessary to burn so many dishes during ancestral worship? The dishes are placed on the table and remain untouched after the ritual. As for lighting incense and candles and burning tin foil, they are even more pointless and simply waste money.

Considering this, should we stop performing ancestral worship altogether? Of course not. If we do not worship our ancestors, future generations will forget them completely. Therefore, I believe that ancestral worship is essential, but we should change the method to avoid all unnecessary expenses. Currently, most people only focus on the formalities of ancestral worship, such as how many dishes to prepare and how much tin foil to burn, without genuine respect. This is fundamentally wrong.

Now, I would like to propose a few methods for improving ancestral worship, for discussion with readers:

(1) Reduce the number of ancestral worship ceremonies from six to two per year, implementing spring and autumn ceremonies, as six is too many and too cumbersome.

(2) Do not light incense or candles, as they serve no purpose.

(3) Do not burn tin foil. To suggest that tin foil is currency for ghosts is a great joke. It is useless. Therefore, I advocate not burning tin foil during ancestral worship to avoid unnecessary expenses.

(4) Replace dishes with fresh flowers and fruits, which are less expensive and more respectful and solemn.

(5) The chief celebrant should be solemn and respectful during ancestral worship, leading the family in recounting the history and achievements of the ancestors, so that future generations will have a lasting and profound impression of their ancestors.

I wonder what the members of this society think of the proposed improvements to ancestral worship. I hope everyone will discuss them.

My Thoughts on Improving Dining Practices 250

— Qixing

To avoid the spread of germs, shared dining should indeed be improved. However, switching to a system of individual servings of one soup and one dish may not suit our traditional appetites. Distributing food in a grid-like platter, like a fruit platter, would be inconvenient. Moreover, changing all bowls and basins to platter style would require notifying artisans nationwide, which is no easy task. For economically disadvantaged families, this is even more unattainable.

Now, in my humble opinion, a compromise between shared and individual dining could avoid financial losses and achieve satisfactory results. Each person could prepare one or two extra bowls and spoons. They could then use their own spoon to serve a portion of the shared dishes into their own bowl. More of the dishes they particularly like could be served. They could then use another spoon to eat. The remaining dishes would stay in the middle of the table, and more could be served later if desired. This would prevent the spread of germs without wasting money. Each family would only need a few extra bowls and spoons. As for the style, why must we copy Western styles? As long as it is practical, we can create our own style. (Respectful dismissal)

Casual Conversation

The Bedbug Revolution 251

— Ren

In the middle of the night, while sleeping in bed, I had a dream. In my dream, a swarm of bedbugs crawled out from the walls, parading and demonstrating on my fleshy mountain. A bedbug, Bedbug A, stood on the tip of my nose and addressed the crowd, seemingly saying:

(Friends, rise up quickly! Last night, I took a bite of human blood. By daybreak, he sprayed me with "Flytox" and burned me with a candle. As a result, more than fifty or sixty of our comrades died. This is outrageous! Are humans so cruel? We must take revenge! We are the blood-sucking party, created by God. If we want to survive, we must strive hard and unite with mosquitoes, fleas, lice, and flies to resist humans.

We are the weaklings of all creatures. We have no other desires besides sucking a mouthful of blood. Humans, on the other hand, are not only terrifying eating parties but also have other insatiable desires besides eating. They refuse our meager nightly requests and want to eliminate us and drive us out. We have been oppressed by humans for thousands of years!)

I felt something crawling on my body, but I was still dreaming. Bedbug B, hearing Bedbug A's speech, eagerly climbed onto my left arm, continuing the speech.

(According to the teachings of Sakyamuni, all creatures should be equal. Therefore, his disciples, the monks, are the most loving. We often suck their blood, but they never complain or resort to killing. However, we cannot just suck their blood because the monks are easy to bully. We should launch a general attack on our abusive enemies!)

(Friends, rise up quickly! For the survival of our species, let us start the blood-sucking party revolution!)

After Bedbug B finished speaking, the crowd applauded. One of the largest and reddest bedbugs, walking unsteadily, climbed onto my shoulder and shouted to other species:

(Mosquitoes, fleas, lice, and flies! Rise up together and bring cholera, plague, and other infectious diseases to the humans. Use them as weapons to declare war on them! Because we are the weaklings of all creatures, we must unite to maintain the status of the blood-sucking party!)

I felt extremely itchy and could not bear to be disturbed any longer. I woke up from the dream. I wondered how I could have such a strange dream. It was not yet dawn. I turned on the electric light, rubbed my eyes, and looked around like a detective. Something was wrong! My whole body was covered with lumps, swollen unevenly, like steamed corn. Red blood-sucking parties were parading on the walls in formation. Furthermore, mosquitoes were playing victory music, extending their bayonets, and charging at me. Fleas and flies were working together, issuing general mobilization orders. I had no choice but to escape that room and let them have their revolution.

Notice to Su Fang: I have read your letter, and the planned project is quite appropriate. However, there are still points to consider. Please come to the library at 3 or 4 PM today or tomorrow to discuss everything in person. Otherwise, I will reply in the newspaper.
